    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";

          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

  <span id="freeText2811773114377438351" style="display:none">In this immensely powerful, lyrical and skillfully narrated novel, set in southern Italy, nine year-old Michele discovers a secret so momentous, so terrible, that he daren’t tell anyone about it. Read an exclusive excerpt at BookBrowse today.<br /><br />The hottest summer of the twentieth century. A tiny community of five houses in the middle of wheat fields. While the adults shelter indoors, six children venture out on their bikes across the scorched, deserted countryside.<br /><br />In the midst of that sea of golden wheat, nine year-old Michele Amitrano discovers a secret so momentous, so terrible, that he daren’t tell anyone about it. To come to terms with it he will have to draw strength from his own imagination and sense of humanity. The reader witnesses a dual story: the one that is seen through Michele's eyes, and the tragedy involving the adults of this isolated hamlet. The result is an immensely powerful, lyrical and skillfully narrated novel, its atmosphere reminiscent of Tom Sawyer, Stephen King's Stand By Me and Italo Calvino's Italian Fairy Tales. <br /><br />This is Ammaniti's third book, but his first to be published in the USA.</span>

      </div>
</div>

<div id="review_75282020" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/75282020" />
    <a title="Lori" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2211350-lori"><img alt="Lori" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1272542911p2/2211350.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/75282020?book_show_action=true">Oct 21, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lori" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lori" href="/user/show/2211350-lori">Lori</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer75282020" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17383012133491302042">I'm not sure how to describe this book. Is it a shattering of innocence, a coming of age story, a mystery, a suspense novel or is it all of these? I was drawn into the story immediately by the short terse prose, the descriptions of the countryside and the dialogue and actions of the young children in the story. Ammaniti, has captured with accuracy the actions and thoughts of a child who is caught in an adult situation. As the reader you are viewing the events from the eyes of nine year old Miche</span>
  <span id="freeText17383012133491302042" style="display:none">I'm not sure how to describe this book. Is it a shattering of innocence, a coming of age story, a mystery, a suspense novel or is it all of these? I was drawn into the story immediately by the short terse prose, the descriptions of the countryside and the dialogue and actions of the young children in the story. Ammaniti, has captured with accuracy the actions and thoughts of a child who is caught in an adult situation. As the reader you are viewing the events from the eyes of nine year old Michelle and you feel the same confusion and detachment that he does when placed in a situation where an incredible event is occuring. As he learns more and sees more from the actions of his parents and the other adults around him be begins to understand what is really happening and can no longer remain detached. He can no longer remain neutral, he must act. The book moves along at a quick pace and ends in a nail biting climax. This was a good story with beautiful detail and a realistic portrayal of a nine year olds reactions and thoughts. I really enjoyed this book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17383012133491302042" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_206877971" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/206877971" />
    <a title="Joselito Honestly and Brilliantly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2190636-joselito-honestly-and-brilliantly"><img alt="Joselito Honestly and Brilliantly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1349701607p2/2190636.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/206877971?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joselito Honestly and Brilliantly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joselito Honestly and Brilliantly" href="/user/show/2190636-joselito-honestly-and-brilliantly">Joselito Honestly and Brilliantly</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer206877971" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12473252096194793024">A real horror. Evil is committed in pursuit of the "good", the victims are innocent and young, their innocence lost in the most painful way possible, and the story ends without any expectation of redemption or happiness for anyone.<br/><br/>And what a unique and brilliant narration! The author inhabits the mind of a nine-year-old boy and tells the story like a real nine-year-old. Reminded me of Esther Freud's "Hideous Kinky" but with really something extraordinary: it doesn't take Niccolo Ammaniti whole p</span>
  <span id="freeText12473252096194793024" style="display:none">A real horror. Evil is committed in pursuit of the "good", the victims are innocent and young, their innocence lost in the most painful way possible, and the story ends without any expectation of redemption or happiness for anyone.<br /><br />And what a unique and brilliant narration! The author inhabits the mind of a nine-year-old boy and tells the story like a real nine-year-old. Reminded me of Esther Freud's "Hideous Kinky" but with really something extraordinary: it doesn't take Niccolo Ammaniti whole paragraphs to jolt his readers. He does it with just one or two short sentences, often when his fictive boy narrator makes a wrong perception of something (which at first seemed real). Then all that the boy has heard, felt and seen he ties them up in the end, like a bundle of hard wires, then hits you with it in the head leaving you dazed.<br /><br />Now thank me for not giving away the plot which, by itself, had it even been badly presented, would have netted five stars from me. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12473252096194793024" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_126771665" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/126771665" />
    <a title="Traveller" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3145526-traveller"><img alt="Traveller" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1423246742p2/3145526.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/126771665?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Traveller" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Traveller" href="/user/show/3145526-traveller">Traveller</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3145526-traveller?shelf=1001-books">1001-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3145526-traveller?shelf=translated">translated</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer126771665" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10737386749096586821">A poignant coming of age story about the loss of innocence of a rural Italian boy. <br/>The tale is told with enough balance as to be emotionally and intellectually engaging without being overly sentimental.<br/><br/>The style comes across as so effortless and the plot is so well handled, that one almost feels as if this could very well really have happened, which makes the chilling and ironic conclusion feel even more shocking and resonant.<br/><br/>..and since truth is stranger than fiction, who knows, perhaps it did </span>
  <span id="freeText10737386749096586821" style="display:none">A poignant coming of age story about the loss of innocence of a rural Italian boy. <br />The tale is told with enough balance as to be emotionally and intellectually engaging without being overly sentimental.<br /><br />The style comes across as so effortless and the plot is so well handled, that one almost feels as if this could very well really have happened, which makes the chilling and ironic conclusion feel even more shocking and resonant.<br /><br />..and since truth is stranger than fiction, who knows, perhaps it did happen; and in a certain sense, it did. The novel is apparently partly based on real-life historical events that took place in 1970's Italy.<br /><br />Although the events that take place is the stuff of crime fiction and thrillers, it's given a fresh 'take' by being told from the point-of-view of the young protagonist who finds himself initially 'outside' the events that eventually rob him of his innocence and introduce him into the harsh world of adult reality.<br /><br />What makes it really stand out from your general run-of-the-mill thriller though, is the insight that Mr Ammaniti shows into the psychology and souls of the characters he brings to life in this deftly-told novel.<br /> <br />Ammaniti poignantly brings to life the mind of an innocent child through the protagonist's initial interpretations of events; and it is a stomach-churning and heart-wrenching process to travel with young Michele into the realization of what is actually going on.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10737386749096586821" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_924468876" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/924468876" />
    <a title="Debbie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8665845-debbie"><img alt="Debbie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1334166735p2/8665845.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/924468876?book_show_action=true">Apr 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debbie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debbie" href="/user/show/8665845-debbie">Debbie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8665845-debbie?shelf=mostly-not-set-in-u-s">mostly-not-set-in-u-s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8665845-debbie?shelf=kids-teens-good-bad">kids-teens-good-bad</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8665845-debbie?shelf=favorite-thrillers">favorite-thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8665845-debbie?shelf=cultural">cultural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8665845-debbie?shelf=runners-up-2012-through-2019">runners-up-2012-through-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8665845-debbie?shelf=crime-and-or-madness">crime-and-or-madness</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer924468876" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10755459162588106929">Despite its title, I’m scared and so is Michele, the 9-year-old narrator of this suspenseful story. It’s fast paced and wild, and you can’t help but be pulled in immediately and with full heart and soul.<br/> <br/>Ammaniti knows how to create a grim story that has a loveable, heroic boy at its center. And he knows how to keep you sitting on the edge of your seat. The book is scary, but addictive. It reads like a nightmarish fairytale. There’s good versus evil all over the place. There’s one small good guy</span>
  <span id="freeText10755459162588106929" style="display:none">Despite its title, I’m scared and so is Michele, the 9-year-old narrator of this suspenseful story. It’s fast paced and wild, and you can’t help but be pulled in immediately and with full heart and soul.<br /> <br />Ammaniti knows how to create a grim story that has a loveable, heroic boy at its center. And he knows how to keep you sitting on the edge of your seat. The book is scary, but addictive. It reads like a nightmarish fairytale. There’s good versus evil all over the place. There’s one small good guy against a slew of big bad guys. And Michele is constantly being exposed to terrifying situations. For example, I died (along with Michele) when his mother insisted that a scary and gross old man would be sharing Michele’s tiny bedroom.<br /><br />Michele stumbles upon a criminal secret and then spends his time frantically trying to help right the wrong. There is much urgent bike riding as he crashes through the wheat fields in the sweltering heat in Italy. We’re routing for him the whole way, but we share his fear that things could get uglier at any second. And they do, repeatedly. Michele is scared, but he’s also brave and determined to make things right, hindered again and again by the evil adults who hold the power.<br /> <br />Michele’s innocence, combined with the impact of the horrific discovery, affect his perception of reality. He begins questioning everyone’s motives and the basic goodness of people. In a minor scene, when he sees his friend dunking her dog in a disgustingly murky pond, he thinks she is killing him. Michele rescues the dog, and the girl insists she was just trying to wash off ticks. Always the helper, Michele then proceeds to remove the ticks. (Ammaniti gives us the gross and graphic details; and we keep watching, the same way we keep watching a car accident.) But was she really trying to kill the dog, or was Michele just being paranoid? Did he save the dog’s life, or was he merely a friend who helped remove some ticks? Ammaniti is a genius at setting up such ambiguous realities.<br /><br />I have four complaints. First, I didn’t think this book was quite as tight as “Me and You,” but that’s only because I’m not a fan of scenery (and I know many people will argue that describing the setting was necessary in order to create the right atmosphere). Second, the translation was poor in the first half of the book. In several cases, the translator used the Italian word instead of the English equivalent—it seemed more a sign of laziness than lack of skill, since some words seemed like they would be easy to translate. Third, even though the ending was clever and dramatic, I thought it was too abrupt. I would have liked more closure. Fourth, I had trouble buying the fact that there was a whole slew of bad guys—including people you would expect to be good guys. I’m just not sure that worked.<br /><br />I give it a 4.6--I knocked off a tenth of a point for each of my four complaints. It’s darker than “Me and You,” but that didn’t stop me from loving it. Wait till you learn about “wash bears.” I hope more people discover this author; he’s a gem. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10755459162588106929" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5204784-vonia?shelf=child-s-perspective">child-s-perspective</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5204784-vonia?shelf=siblings">siblings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5204784-vonia?shelf=parenting">parenting</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5204784-vonia?shelf=made-into-film">made-into-film</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5204784-vonia?shelf=murder-crime">murder-crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5204784-vonia?shelf=friendships">friendships</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5204784-vonia?shelf=morality">morality</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1605034077" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3965476409048724176">My second book from Nicolo Ammanati. The first was "Me and You". "I'm Not Scared" was able to rectify my complaints about the first (lack of believability, focus on only one character's development, rushed story and rash examinations of important issues), but things I was impressed by in "Me and You" fell by the wayside here (insightful emotional examination, keeping the reader's interest, no unnecessary scenes). <br/><br/>"Spine-tingling"? I hate to say this (because I love his writings, I really do, but</span>
  <span id="freeText3965476409048724176" style="display:none">My second book from Nicolo Ammanati. The first was "Me and You". "I'm Not Scared" was able to rectify my complaints about the first (lack of believability, focus on only one character's development, rushed story and rash examinations of important issues), but things I was impressed by in "Me and You" fell by the wayside here (insightful emotional examination, keeping the reader's interest, no unnecessary scenes). <br /><br />"Spine-tingling"? I hate to say this (because I love his writings, I really do, but neither of the books I have read by him have all the components necessary for that really good book), but not so much. I lost interest a few different times. I feel like the suspense waned as the book continued, with not much explanation for different events, except that Michele was unable to learn everything from the secretive adults. <br /><br />Believability? That a group of men in a small town, one of which is our narrator's father, together manage to kidnap a nine year old boy for ransom? Yes, likely it has happened before. That they are all mostly good people? Certainly. That the wives are mostly in on it and if not condoning, have accepted it? Maybe not so much, but given the time period, yes. And it is the extremely rare but very possible events that make the best fiction. After all, real life has the best stories. One could never make some of that stuff up. <br /><br />The book was good, but not great. Pacing issues, character depth focused almost entirely on the narrator (understandable, as it is not an omniscient voice, but makes the important point that this particular story may have been better served if it were), and, most importantly, anticlimactic. I was very upset with the ending. The vagueness of it, the ridiculousness. It left me feeling cheated.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3965476409048724176" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_800249372" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/800249372" />
    <a title="Diane S ☔" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4159922-diane-s"><img alt="Diane S ☔" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598402138p2/4159922.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/800249372?book_show_action=true">Dec 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diane S ☔" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diane S ☔" href="/user/show/4159922-diane-s">Diane S ☔</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer800249372" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11383151116139102155">Set during the heat wave in the summer of 1978, in rural Italy nine year old Michele and his friends pretty much have the countryside to themselves. The parents stay in and try to alleviate the heat in whatever ways they can. Michele is only concerned about today, like most children and does not yet think about the wider picture, world events or other things that have affected his town. His only concern is having to drag his little sister everywhere, his friend Salvatore and the unelected leader</span>
  <span id="freeText11383151116139102155" style="display:none">Set during the heat wave in the summer of 1978, in rural Italy nine year old Michele and his friends pretty much have the countryside to themselves. The parents stay in and try to alleviate the heat in whatever ways they can. Michele is only concerned about today, like most children and does not yet think about the wider picture, world events or other things that have affected his town. His only concern is having to drag his little sister everywhere, his friend Salvatore and the unelected leader of the group who can be very cruel. Yet one day, an top of a hill and in a old house everything for Michele will change in an instant.<br /><br />Almost from the beginning, I felt a palpable tension in this book, the heat, the barren countryside and the short sentences all added to this feeling. I found this to be a gripping read of lost innocence as what Michele finds causes him to mistrust those he previously trusted the most, even his own father. By the ending things have happened that cannot be undone and I was left thinking, what a heavy price there was to pay for trying to do the right thing. I was so proud of this little boy for going the extra mile for what he thought was right. Rather short novel but awfully though provoking.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11383151116139102155" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1359790006" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11503265208058766915">I read this book for my Italian class. Reading in another language, especially it being my first time reading a full-length novel in Italian in this case, was a really rewarding experience and it allowed me to experience one of my favorite activities in a completely different way. I read this with a pencil in hand and circled all of the words I didn't understand (there were quite a few). I hope to do this again in the near future, with Italian and other languages, because I really enjoyed the ch</span>
  <span id="freeText11503265208058766915" style="display:none">I read this book for my Italian class. Reading in another language, especially it being my first time reading a full-length novel in Italian in this case, was a really rewarding experience and it allowed me to experience one of my favorite activities in a completely different way. I read this with a pencil in hand and circled all of the words I didn't understand (there were quite a few). I hope to do this again in the near future, with Italian and other languages, because I really enjoyed the challenge. The book itself was quite wonderful, riddled with aspects of magical realism, though quite a few questions, it seemed to me, were left unanswered. By the end I was both shocked and confused, leaving me with mixed feelings that I hope to clear up by watching the movie adaptation.</span>

<div id="review_148551739" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/148551739" />
    <a title="Tracey Allen at Carpe Librum" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4986986-tracey-allen-at-carpe-librum"><img alt="Tracey Allen at Carpe Librum" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459779189p2/4986986.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/148551739?book_show_action=true">Feb 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tracey Allen at Carpe Librum" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tracey Allen at Carpe Librum" href="/user/show/4986986-tracey-allen-at-carpe-librum">Tracey Allen at Carpe Librum</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer148551739&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer148551739" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16332673322881662723">I'd been looking forward to reading this book for quite a while. Knowing it was about a young child who discovers a boy being kept hostage/prisoner in a hole and and what unfolds next was enough to significantly grab my attention.<br/><br/>Reading it however was a completely different experience and a major disappointment. Set in Italy, the translation from Italian to English is extremely noticeable and often interrupts the natural flow of the descriptive sections of the novel. The setting and location fe</span>
  <span id="freeText16332673322881662723" style="display:none">I'd been looking forward to reading this book for quite a while. Knowing it was about a young child who discovers a boy being kept hostage/prisoner in a hole and and what unfolds next was enough to significantly grab my attention.<br /><br />Reading it however was a completely different experience and a major disappointment. Set in Italy, the translation from Italian to English is extremely noticeable and often interrupts the natural flow of the descriptive sections of the novel. The setting and location felt isolated to me and not well developed. The discovery of the kidnapped boy in the beginning of the book was the most exciting part, and then it was all down hill from there.<br /><br />The middle of the book was frustrating as I struggled with the direction the 9 year old boy was taking with his new found knowledge. There was a slight surprise in the circumstances surrounding the kidnapping which I thought was building to an exciting big 'reveal' at the end which unfortunately didn't happen. The ending was very predictable and reminiscent of 'The Boy in the Striped Pajamas', although I'm happy to report that it appears this novel was published first.<br /><br />In fact the ending was so lacking an explanation for the kidnapping that I thought I must be missing a page or two. Perhaps it had fallen out of the library book. This idea kept me going for a few minutes, and led me to the ever faithful Amazon and Google.<br /><br />I guess you could say this is proof of a terrible ending and a great disappointment. The ending went beyond ambiguous to just plain lacking.<br /><br />This was a terrible read, and I wouldn't recommend this book to anyone.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16332673322881662723" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11868878793224280786">Well, <i>he</i> may not be scared but call me utterly terrifed.   <span id="freeText11868878793224280786" style="display:none">Well, <i>he</i> may not be scared but call me utterly terrifed. I find it hard to believe the book could be better or even equal to the film which I've seen twice and I wasn't any less scared the second time.<br /><br />I must confess that I've done no more than flick through the book and check the odd scene here and there. Sorry, book, but the visual spectacle of the film simply outdoes in spades anything you can do in words. <br /><br />The first thing I wanted to do when I saw this film was give it to my father. It was a story of what his life would have been like if my grandfather hadn't made the decision to leave Calabria for something better - Australia, as it happened. Since my father bitterly resents his childhood, I thought it might do him good to see how bad it might have been.<br /><br />But I couldn't make myself do this. I was plain scared of how terrified he would be. I was scared of the demons it would awaken inside him.<br /><br />See the movie if you can, it's brilliant. And don't be put off by my terror. It is also sweet and gentle, and a lovely reflection on childhood.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer38375135" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1399476898387598847">This is one of the best thrillers I have read this year. This book is translated from the Italian version. The suspense in this book was not overpowering. It’s not one of those fast pace modern day thrillers. <br/><br/>It opens in a small isolated Italian town where a 10 year old boy discovers a secret in an abandoned farmhouse. He struggles to keep it a secret and to make sense out of what he has discovered. The descriptions of the prairie and the region are so wonderful that I could actually imagine bei</span>
  <span id="freeText1399476898387598847" style="display:none">This is one of the best thrillers I have read this year. This book is translated from the Italian version. The suspense in this book was not overpowering. It’s not one of those fast pace modern day thrillers. <br /><br />It opens in a small isolated Italian town where a 10 year old boy discovers a secret in an abandoned farmhouse. He struggles to keep it a secret and to make sense out of what he has discovered. The descriptions of the prairie and the region are so wonderful that I could actually imagine being there. I could actually feel the oppressive heat and the sensation of being stuck in a place where nothing ever happens. The end is really sad. <br /><br />I urge you to read this. This is one of the very few books where you actually feel the fear of the little boy, the kind of fear that reaches deep down into your bones and grips you. For people who love good thrillers with good writing, this book is for you. I cannot recommend it enough. F.A.N.T.A.S.T.I.C.<br /></span>

  <span id="freeText6572374219024032596" style="display:none">Nine-year-old Michele is the narrator. He lives in Southern Italy in a small settlement of four houses surrounded by farmland. He has a small circle of friends, his family is poor but he and his sister live in a loving home.<br />Michele stumbles upon a boy of his own age who has been kidnapped. What follows is Michele coming to grips with a boy being kept in a hole. Somehow there is an apparent normality as the entire settlement seems to be involved. <br />Written in the first person and narrated by a nine year old, the language is simple and Michele's thinking quite believable for his age and his knowledge of the world. There was tension in the storyline, loyalty towards friends and family tested and a fitting climax to be a well told story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6572374219024032596" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Told in the voice of a 9 year-old boy, it’s a vivid portrayal of childhood combined with a deeply disturbing discovery of what it means to be adult. This is gripping and unforgettable storytelling with a convincing juvenile narrator.</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer9822234487936603019">“Stop all this talk about monsters, Michele. Monsters don’t exist. It’s men you should be afraid of, not monsters.”<br/><br/>This coming of age story is translated from the Italian by Jonathan Hunt. <br/><br/>A bunch of kids are out riding their bikes in a tiny village in Southern Italy. On a dare one of them enters an abandoned farmhouse and stumbles upon something horrible. <br/><br/>The protagonist of this story is a nine year old boy, and themes explored include the loss of childhood innocence, and the confusion of tryin</span>
  <span id="freeText9822234487936603019" style="display:none">“Stop all this talk about monsters, Michele. Monsters don’t exist. It’s men you should be afraid of, not monsters.”<br /><br />This coming of age story is translated from the Italian by Jonathan Hunt. <br /><br />A bunch of kids are out riding their bikes in a tiny village in Southern Italy. On a dare one of them enters an abandoned farmhouse and stumbles upon something horrible. <br /><br />The protagonist of this story is a nine year old boy, and themes explored include the loss of childhood innocence, and the confusion of trying to make sense of the adult world. I really liked the setting, and the sense of place in this story. Much of the confusion for the reader makes a certain amount of sense as we only know what the nine year old knows - though there are some things we, the adult reader, understand that he does not. While I liked it, it didn't get a higher rating because I wasn't really sucked into the story and things seemed to happen at an emotional distance, though maybe that's because the character is only nine. The buildup is slow which made the rushed ending seem out of place. I for one did like that final scene, a tad predictable yes, but it was good nonetheless.</span>

<div id="review_266611595" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/266611595" />
    <a title="Elizabeth (Alaska)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2026178-elizabeth-alaska"><img alt="Elizabeth (Alaska)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1304966095p2/2026178.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/266611595?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elizabeth (Alaska)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elizabeth (Alaska)" href="/user/show/2026178-elizabeth-alaska">Elizabeth (Alaska)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2026178-elizabeth-alaska?shelf=1001-books">1001-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer266611595" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12249489258741374434">I have no idea why this is on the 1001 books list. The description here at Goodreads says it is a coming of age story. If it is, then I don't know the definition of the term. The narrator is 9 years old, does not get older in the story, and though he gains understanding about the circumstances in the novel, does not seem to gain understanding about life in general.<br/><br/>I found nothing particularly scary about the book. In the first few pages the narrator tells us something that happens to him 10 year</span>
  <span id="freeText12249489258741374434" style="display:none">I have no idea why this is on the 1001 books list. The description here at Goodreads says it is a coming of age story. If it is, then I don't know the definition of the term. The narrator is 9 years old, does not get older in the story, and though he gains understanding about the circumstances in the novel, does not seem to gain understanding about life in general.<br /><br />I found nothing particularly scary about the book. In the first few pages the narrator tells us something that happens to him 10 years in the future. He also reflects on what his town was like at the time of the story as if it is in the past. Armed with this knowledge, the reader should know he survives the novel's circumstances, and there is no reason to be afraid for him. And, of course, it's a first person narrative. I think I heard there were a couple of first person novels where the person dies, but I had no reason to expect this to be one of them.<br /><br />The prose is too simple for my tastes. Yes, the narrator is 9 years old. The sentence structure is appropriate for that age, but there were bits of vocabulary that didn't fit a 9 year old. So, from me, the author gets marked down on the writing itself. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12249489258741374434" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2285606233" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2285606233" />
    <a title="Andy Weston" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/313206-andy-weston"><img alt="Andy Weston" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1190073185p2/313206.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2285606233?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andy Weston" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andy Weston" href="/user/show/313206-andy-weston">Andy Weston</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/313206-andy-weston?shelf=italy">italy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/313206-andy-weston?shelf=translated">translated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/313206-andy-weston?shelf=crime">crime</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2285606233" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18018982969902358756">Ammaniti chooses a 9 year old boy as narrator and hero of his story of a ‘kidnapping gone wrong’ in a rural part of southern Italy in a hot summer of the late 1970s. <br/><i> We could do whatever we liked. No cars ever went by. There were no dangers. And the grown-ups stayed shut up indoors, like toads waiting for the heat to die down. </i> <br/><br/>Of great appeal is what goes on in the mind of a boy of that age. It is story of innocence lost, as he is just beginning to sort out right from wrong, and real fears fro</span>
  <span id="freeText18018982969902358756" style="display:none">Ammaniti chooses a 9 year old boy as narrator and hero of his story of a ‘kidnapping gone wrong’ in a rural part of southern Italy in a hot summer of the late 1970s. <br /><i> We could do whatever we liked. No cars ever went by. There were no dangers. And the grown-ups stayed shut up indoors, like toads waiting for the heat to die down. </i> <br /><br />Of great appeal is what goes on in the mind of a boy of that age. It is story of innocence lost, as he is just beginning to sort out right from wrong, and real fears from imagined ones, monsters from pigs, dogs from the <i> lords of the hill </i>. His father tells him, <i> it’s men you should be afraid of, not monsters. </i>, but the adults play distant roles, it is a story about childhood, written for adults. Until the last page it is an exciting and unpredictable thriller. It’s not easy for the reader to anticipate the actions of a 9 year old, and that is a reason why it works so well. <br /><br />I especially enjoyed the dramatic and eloquent descriptions of the rural setting, and it’s contribution to the aura and mood that is created. <br /><br /><i> We were cycling, all of us, just like the first time, towards the hill. <br />We rode rode in single file. Only my sister was missing. <br />The atmosphere was close and the sky was an unnatural scarlet colour. The clouds, previously massed on the horizon, were now gathered above us and jostling each other like hordes of Huns before a battle. They were large and somber. The sun was opaque and turbid as if a filter was screening it. The air was neither hot nor cold, but it was windy. At the sides of the road and on the fields the hay was packed up in bales, which were arranged like pawns on a chessboard. Where the combine harvester hadn’t passed, long waves formed, ruffling the wheat. <br /><br /><br />Those shouts were like the spitting of green lizards. Green lizards, when they can’t get away and you’re about to catch them, open their mouths, swell up and spit and try to scare you because they’re more scared of you. </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="18018982969902358756" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Petra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/72638153-petra"><img alt="Petra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603342029p2/72638153.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2698056757?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petra" href="/user/show/72638153-petra">Petra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10912726257155027096">I had to read this book for my Italian oral exam this week. I've studied Italian for less than a year, so I'm already proud I got the gist of this and definitely cannot comment on the language. <br/><br/>The story was actually really interesting and gripping for the most part. The hottest summer in Southern Italy ever. The kids go out to play in the fields all day.   <span id="freeText10912726257155027096" style="display:none">I had to read this book for my Italian oral exam this week. I've studied Italian for less than a year, so I'm already proud I got the gist of this and definitely cannot comment on the language. <br /><br />The story was actually really interesting and gripping for the most part. The hottest summer in Southern Italy ever. The kids go out to play in the fields all day. Nine-year old Michele has to go into an abandoned farmhouse on a dare and finds a kid his age stuck in a hole, presumably kidnapped. The plot unfolds from there. <br /><br />As I said, this book was actually pretty good- until the end. There was absolutely NO resolution whatsoever. It wasn't even an open-ended story. You just never found out what any of the evil characters' motivations were, why they did what they did, what actually HAPPENED at the end. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ <br />The novel ends with the kid getting shot by his dad, but you already know he doesn't die because he narrates the story as an adult. I want to know what the fuck happened after he discovers his parents are responsible for the kidnapping of Filippo. Especially since you never found out why they did it. The rich lawyer was involved, so, not money? Why THAT kid? His parents weren't famous. Why did Filippo think his parents were dead? This book started out raising a million great questions, but then failed to answer a single one of them. SO DUMB. <br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />So yeah, I'm mostly just angry because it actually felt like the author had a great idea for a story, but never thought about how to end it. It doesn't feel like everything was purposefully left open-ended, it just feels like lazy/bad storytelling. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10912726257155027096" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2386804-mj-nicholls?shelf=southern-europe">southern-europe</a>,

              <span id="reviewTextContainer184658112" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer960561640915674209">A small-town kidnapping tale, told from the POV of an ickle boy. What vexes me about narrators close to the child's perspective is that the narrator is usually a grown-up narrating their childhood from twenty or so years on. The same is true here: the grown-up Michele is narrating his childhood twenty-odd years later. My question: why would a grown-up write his story with such a close childhood POV <i>unless</i> he was a writer who had consciously taken that decision to sustain such a narrative positio</span>
  <span id="freeText960561640915674209" style="display:none">A small-town kidnapping tale, told from the POV of an ickle boy. What vexes me about narrators close to the child's perspective is that the narrator is usually a grown-up narrating their childhood from twenty or so years on. The same is true here: the grown-up Michele is narrating his childhood twenty-odd years later. My question: why would a grown-up write his story with such a close childhood POV <i>unless</i> he was a writer who had consciously taken that decision to sustain such a narrative position and style? Answer me that, Consuelo!<br /><br />Regardless, this reads basically like a film script: extremely fast action, a new paragraph break every sentence, picturesque Italian scenery, manipulative child-beating. Someone ought to make a film version. Oh wait . . . they . . . they . . . they'd have to pay the writer. Never mind then. </span>

<div id="review_2476710765" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2476710765" />
    <a title="Michael Cayley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20845184-michael-cayley"><img alt="Michael Cayley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1370019081p2/20845184.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2476710765?book_show_action=true">Jul 31, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael Cayley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael Cayley" href="/user/show/20845184-michael-cayley">Michael Cayley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20845184-michael-cayley?shelf=general-fiction">general-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2476710765" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5594801154543394542">This is a vivid portrayal of children in impoverished rural South Italy caught up in the ruthless actions of an adult world they do not fully understand. It is told from the viewpoint of 9-year-old Michele. He and a gang stumble across a derelict house. As a forfeit he clambers up to the first floor and makes his dangerous way across it, to drop down the other side of the building. There he comes across something which he dare not tell the other children about, and which haunts him in the weeks </span>
  <span id="freeText5594801154543394542" style="display:none">This is a vivid portrayal of children in impoverished rural South Italy caught up in the ruthless actions of an adult world they do not fully understand. It is told from the viewpoint of 9-year-old Michele. He and a gang stumble across a derelict house. As a forfeit he clambers up to the first floor and makes his dangerous way across it, to drop down the other side of the building. There he comes across something which he dare not tell the other children about, and which haunts him in the weeks to come. The story moves to a violent climax with the inevitability of an ancient Greek tragedy.<br /><br />What makes this short book so good is the way the author has got inside the mindset of a child. The rough-and-tumble of life as a child in this rural environment comes over well, as does the sometimes casual cruelty of the young gang. The style is appropriate for a boy of this age. Sentences are almost all short, with few subordinate clauses, and verbs are often omitted. Dialogue uses simple language. The narrative moves forward quite quickly. And the descriptions of the rustic setting are vivid.<br /><br />Thoroughly recommended.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5594801154543394542" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2901959252" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2901959252" />
    <a title="Spencer Fancutt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/63297537-spencer-fancutt"><img alt="Spencer Fancutt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1484966029p2/63297537.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2901959252?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Spencer Fancutt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Spencer Fancutt" href="/user/show/63297537-spencer-fancutt">Spencer Fancutt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781782117155" href="/book/show/32321923-i-m-not-scared">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2901959252" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16227514231302635924">Great little pageturner. Ammaniti delivers a pitch-perfect coming-of-age thriller impossible not to burn through. The close feels too abrupt, but the plot has a reader going at such a compulsive speed, there is hardly the time to put the brakes on.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3241859445" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3241859445" />
    <a title="Pallavi Bichu" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/65019068-pallavi-bichu"><img alt="Pallavi Bichu" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589930917p2/65019068.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3241859445?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pallavi Bichu" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pallavi Bichu" href="/user/show/65019068-pallavi-bichu">Pallavi Bichu</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3241859445" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10443568006200145624">A fast-paced, easy read. The protagonist and the mystery are well-etched out, if a bit simplistic. Unfortunately not the best foray into Italian literature, as this seems to be a pop thriller fiction, but the descriptions of the Italian countryside left me wanting more.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('tEbwU+lw7EEdDZ2Xbnhon9C3E19WELBh7S2/uShPL2KGOnopOR6DeLr6fNGnz7FUSay2fqTiq3/v8+dmYCNYsQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('SGaOJKpTuEKUZsf+MG9NcFjhDU+2pPrqCN5jBTk58sx6GgReej3XezORJrj52JS7wfqobkRW4fQKADvacVWFHw==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13015883067324034748">Niccolò Ammaniti was born in Rome in 1966. He has written three novels and a collection of short stories. He won the prestigious Italian Viareggio-Repaci Prize for Fiction with his bestselling novel I'm Not Scared, which has been translated into thirty-five languages.</span>
